<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Vanessa Hudgens</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>

<p><b>Vanessa Anne Hudgens</b> (born December 14, 1988) is an American actress and singer. Hudgens rose to prominence playing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gabriella_Montez" title="Gabriella Montez">Gabriella Montez</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High_School_Musical_(film_series)" title="High School Musical (film series)"><i>High School Musical</i> series</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> Hudgens has also appeared in various films and television series for the <a href="/wiki/Disney_Channel" title="Disney Channel">Disney Channel</a>. She had her feature film debut in the 2003 film <i><a href="/wiki/Thirteen_(2003_film)" title="Thirteen (2003 film)">Thirteen</a></i>, a teenage drama in which Hudgens had a supporting role. She had mainstream success following the release of the <i><a href="/wiki/High_School_Musical" title="High School Musical">High School Musical</a></i> trilogy, and her relationship with co-star <a href="/wiki/Zac_Efron" title="Zac Efron">Zac Efron</a> was heavily publicized. Her appearance in the series helped make her a household name. Songs from the films also charted worldwide, with the song "<a href="/wiki/Breaking_Free" title="Breaking Free">Breaking Free</a>" peaking inside the Top 10 of the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>. This led to Hudgens releasing her debut album, <i><a href="/wiki/V_(Vanessa_Hudgens_album)" title="V (Vanessa Hudgens album)">V</a></i>, on September 26, 2006 which entered the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> at number 24, and was later <a href="/wiki/Music_recording_sales_certification" title="Music recording sales certification">certified gold</a>. Her second album, <i><a href="/wiki/Identified" title="Identified">Identified</a></i>, was released on July 1, 2008 in the United States.</p>
<p>Since the release of her albums and the <i>High School Musical</i> franchise, Hudgens has focused on her acting career. She has appeared in the films <i><a href="/wiki/Bandslam" title="Bandslam">Bandslam</a></i> (2009), <i><a href="/wiki/Beastly_(film)" title="Beastly (film)">Beastly</a></i> (2011), <i><a href="/wiki/Sucker_Punch_(2011_film)" title="Sucker Punch (2011 film)">Sucker Punch</a></i> (2011), <i><a href="/wiki/Journey_2:_The_Mysterious_Island" title="Journey 2: The Mysterious Island">Journey 2: The Mysterious Island</a></i> (2012), <i><a href="/wiki/Spring_Breakers" title="Spring Breakers">Spring Breakers</a></i> (2013), and <i><a href="/wiki/Machete_Kills" title="Machete Kills">Machete Kills</a></i> (2013). She has also played the title role in the <a href="/wiki/Broadway_theatre" title="Broadway theatre">Broadway</a> musical <i><a href="/wiki/Gigi_(musical)#Productions" title="Gigi (musical)">Gigi</a></i> in 2015, and the role of Rizzo in <i><a href="/wiki/Grease:_Live" title="Grease: Live">Grease: Live</a></i> in 2016.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>
<p>Hudgens was born in <a href="/wiki/Salinas,_California" title="Salinas, California">Salinas, California</a>, and lived with her parents along the <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="West Coast of the United States">West Coast</a>, from <a href="/wiki/Oregon" title="Oregon">Oregon</a> to <a href="/wiki/Southern_California" title="Southern California">Southern California</a>. Her mother, Gina (née Guangco), held a succession of office jobs, and her father, Gregory Hudgens, was a <a href="/wiki/Firefighter" title="Firefighter">firefighter</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yahoo_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-yahoo-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-inquirer_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-inquirer-3">[3]</a></sup> She has a younger sister, Stella Hudgens, who is also an actress.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> She was raised as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> Her father was of Irish and <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">Native American</a> descent, and her mother, a native of <a href="/wiki/Manila" title="Manila">Manila</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, is of Filipino descent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-inquirer_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-inquirer-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TeenHollywood_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-TeenHollywood-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> All of her grandparents were musicians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kidzworld_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-kidzworld-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2002.E2.80.9305:_Career_beginnings">2002–05: Career beginnings</span></h3>
<p>Starting at the age of eight, Hudgens performed in musical theater as a singer, and appeared in local productions of <i><a href="/wiki/Carousel_(musical)" title="Carousel (musical)">Carousel</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Wizard_of_Oz_(adaptations)" title="The Wizard of Oz (adaptations)">The Wizard of Oz</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_King_and_I" title="The King and I">The King and I</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Music_Man" title="The Music Man">The Music Man</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Cinderella" title="Cinderella">Cinderella</a></i>, among others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vanbio_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-vanbio-9">[9]</a></sup> Two years after her career in stage plays and musicals, she started auditioning for commercials and television shows, and her family moved to Los Angeles after she won a role in a television commercial.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kidzworld_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-kidzworld-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parade_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-parade-10">[10]</a></sup> Her acting career started at the age of 15, and she briefly attended <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orange_County_High_School_of_the_Arts" title="Orange County High School of the Arts">Orange County High School of the Arts</a>, followed by homeschooling with tutors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hudgens had her first acting role in an episode of the sitcom <i><a href="/wiki/Still_Standing_(TV_series)" title="Still Standing (TV series)">Still Standing</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> in which she portrayed Tiffany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Following her appearance on the series, she guest starred in an episode of the series <i><a href="/wiki/Robbery_Homicide_Division" title="Robbery Homicide Division">Robbery Homicide Division</a></i>, airing on <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a> in 2002. 2003 saw Hudgens making her theatrical debut in the 2003 drama film <i><a href="/wiki/Thirteen_(2003_film)" title="Thirteen (2003 film)">Thirteen</a></i>, in which she had the supporting role of Noel. The film, which revolved around teenager Tracy trying to fit in and getting caught up in the wrong crowd, was somewhat of a commercial success, grossing $10 million worldwide. Despite its minor commercial success, the film received positive critical reviews. It has an 82% "fresh" rating on <a href="/wiki/Rotten_Tomatoes" title="Rotten Tomatoes">Rotten Tomatoes</a>, and <i><a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a></i> called <i>Thirteen</i> the most "powerful of all recent wayward-youth sagas".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Hudgens subsequently landed a role in the 2004 science fiction-adventure film <i><a href="/wiki/Thunderbirds_(2004_film)" title="Thunderbirds (2004 film)">Thunderbirds</a></i>, based on the <a href="/wiki/Thunderbirds_(TV_series)" title="Thunderbirds (TV series)">television series of the same name</a>. Hudgens portrayed the character of Tin-tin. The film was a commercial failure and was strongly criticized for "abandoning the original concepts".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2006.E2.80.9308:_High_School_Musical.2C_V_and_Identified">2006–08: <i>High School Musical</i>, <i>V</i> and <i>Identified</i></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vanessa_Anne_Hudgens,_HSM2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="766" data-file-width="773" height="218" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Vanessa_Anne_Hudgens%2C_HSM2.jpg/220px-Vanessa_Anne_Hudgens%2C_HSM2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Vanessa_Anne_Hudgens%2C_HSM2.jpg/330px-Vanessa_Anne_Hudgens%2C_HSM2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Vanessa_Anne_Hudgens%2C_HSM2.jpg/440px-Vanessa_Anne_Hudgens%2C_HSM2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vanessa_Anne_Hudgens,_HSM2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hudgens performing at the <a href="/wiki/High_School_Musical:_The_Concert" title="High School Musical: The Concert">High School Musical: The Concert</a> in 2007</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2005, Hudgens was cast as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gabriella_Montez" title="Gabriella Montez">Gabriella Montez</a>, one of the lead roles in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Disney_Channel_Original_Movies" title="List of Disney Channel Original Movies">Disney Channel Original Movie</a> <i><a href="/wiki/High_School_Musical" title="High School Musical">High School Musical</a></i>. The film saw Hudgens portraying the new girl at high school who falls for the captain of the basketball team. The two later reveal a passion for singing, and audition for the school play together. Hudgens starred alongside <a href="/wiki/Zac_Efron" title="Zac Efron">Zac Efron</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ashley_Tisdale" title="Ashley Tisdale">Ashley Tisdale</a> in the film,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> the former of which she was partnered up with during the auditioning process due to their "chemistry".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> The film, released on January 20, 2006, was both a critical and commercial success. <i>High School Musical</i> was <a href="/wiki/Disney_Channel" title="Disney Channel">Disney Channel</a>'s most watched film that year with 7.7 million viewers in its premiere broadcast in the US, until August's premiere of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Cheetah_Girls_2" title="The Cheetah Girls 2">The Cheetah Girls 2</a></i>, which achieved 8.1 million viewers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> In the UK, it received 789,000 viewers for its premiere (and 1.2 million viewers overall during the first week), making it the second most watched program for the Disney Channel (UK) of 2006. On December 29, 2006, it became the first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disney_Channel_Original_Movie" title="Disney Channel Original Movie">Disney Channel Original Movie</a> to be broadcast on the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> For the film, Hudgens recorded numerous songs which had commercial success. The song "<a href="/wiki/Breaking_Free" title="Breaking Free">Breaking Free</a>", a duet with Zac Efron, went on to become Hudgens' only Top 10 hit on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> to date, when it peaked at number 4 on the chart. The song also reached number 9 in the UK, her highest chart entry in the country. Following the success of the film, Hudgens began work on her debut album. The project, later revealed to be titled <i>V</i>, was released on September 26, 2006. The album sold 34,000 copies in its first week of release, and debuted at number 24 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> chart in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard.com_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard.com-22">[22]</a></sup> In February 2007, the album was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Certified_gold" title="Certified gold">certified gold</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">RIAA</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1958_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1958-23">[23]</a></sup> As of August 2009, the album has sold 570,000 copies in the U.S.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> It was preceded by two singles, "<a href="/wiki/Come_Back_to_Me_(Vanessa_Hudgens_song)" title="Come Back to Me (Vanessa Hudgens song)">Come Back to Me</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Say_OK" title="Say OK">Say OK</a>", both of which were slightly successful in numerous countries. Both singles received heavy promotion on Disney Channel, with the music videos for both premiering on the channel.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vanessa_Hudgens_3.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="768" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Vanessa_Hudgens_3.jpg/170px-Vanessa_Hudgens_3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Vanessa_Hudgens_3.jpg/255px-Vanessa_Hudgens_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Vanessa_Hudgens_3.jpg/340px-Vanessa_Hudgens_3.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vanessa_Hudgens_3.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hudgens in concert in January 2007</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2007, work on the second film in the <i>High School Musical</i> series began, and Hudgens was confirmed to be returning for the sequel. <i><a href="/wiki/High_School_Musical_2" title="High School Musical 2">High School Musical 2</a></i> was released on August 17, 2007. The premiere was seen by a total of over 17.2 million viewers in the U.S., which is almost 10 million more than its predecessor, making it the highest-rated Disney Channel Movie of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> Disney Channel aired a weekly program called <i>Road to High School Musical 2</i>, beginning on June 8, 2007, and leading up to the premiere of <i>High School Musical 2</i> in August. The show offered viewers a behind-the-scenes look into the production of the movie. The world premiere of the opening number "<a href="/wiki/What_Time_Is_It%3F_(song)" title="What Time Is It? (song)">What Time Is It</a>" was on <a href="/wiki/Radio_Disney" title="Radio Disney">Radio Disney</a> May 25, 2007,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> and similarly "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/You_Are_The_Music_In_Me" title="You Are The Music In Me">You Are The Music In Me</a>" premiered on July 13, 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> The film was generally well received by critics, gaining a score of 77/100 at <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> while it received a generally mixed response of 50% on <a href="/wiki/Rotten_Tomatoes" title="Rotten Tomatoes">Rotten Tomatoes</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a>'</i>s Robert Bianco awarded the film three stars out of four, saying <i>High School Musical 2</i> was "sweet, smart, bursting with talent and energy, and awash in innocence".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> While critics enjoyed the film, they noted that the timing of the movie's premiere seemed odd, premiering just when school was about to start up again, while the movie's plot involved the gang going on summer vacation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> <i>High School Musical 2</i> won the "So Hot Right Now" award at the <a href="/wiki/Nickelodeon_Australian_Kids%27_Choice_Awards_2007" title="Nickelodeon Australian Kids' Choice Awards 2007">Nickelodeon Australian Kids' Choice Awards 2007</a> in which High School Musical cast mate, Zac Efron hosted with <a href="/wiki/The_Veronicas" title="The Veronicas">The Veronicas</a>.</p>
<p>In 2007, Hudgens began work on her second studio album, partly due to the success of the <i>High School Musical</i> franchise. Her second studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Identified" title="Identified">Identified</a></i>, was released on July 1, 2008. It sold 22,000 copies in its first week of release, 12,000 less than that of her previous effort.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Despite the drop in sales, the album debuted at number 23, one spot higher than <i>V</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> The album was preceded by one single, "<a href="/wiki/Sneakernight" title="Sneakernight">Sneakernight</a>", which was her lowest performing single in the US to date. It was a success on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hot_Dance_Club_Songs" title="Hot Dance Club Songs">Hot Dance Club Songs</a> chart in the US, where it peaked at number 8.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Following the commercial failure of the album, it was announced that Hudgens had parted ways with <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Records" title="Hollywood Records">Hollywood Records</a>. Hudgens went on to reprise her role as Gabriella in the 2008 sequel <i><a href="/wiki/High_School_Musical_3:_Senior_Year" title="High School Musical 3: Senior Year">High School Musical 3: Senior Year</a></i>, the first film from the franchise to be released theatrically. It opened at number one at the North American box office in October 2008, earning $42 million in its first weekend, which broke the record previously held by <i><a href="/wiki/Mamma_Mia!_(film)" title="Mamma Mia! (film)">Mamma Mia!</a></i> for the biggest opening by a musical.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> The film finished with $252 million worldwide, which exceeded Disney's expectations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2009.E2.80.9314:_Focus_on_films">2009–14: Focus on films</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vanessa_Hudgens_2011.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2818" data-file-width="1942" height="247" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Vanessa_Hudgens_2011.jpg/170px-Vanessa_Hudgens_2011.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Vanessa_Hudgens_2011.jpg/255px-Vanessa_Hudgens_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Vanessa_Hudgens_2011.jpg/340px-Vanessa_Hudgens_2011.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vanessa_Hudgens_2011.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hudgens at the MyHabit launch at Skylight West Studios in May 2011</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Following the completion of the <i>High School Musical</i> series, Hudgens confirmed that she was taking a break from her music career to focus more on acting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> She played a supporting role in a musical comedy <i><a href="/wiki/Bandslam" title="Bandslam">Bandslam</a></i>, which was released theatrically on August 14, 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-weird_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-weird-39">[39]</a></sup> Hudgens plays "Sa5m", a 15-year-old awkward freshman with untapped talents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> Although <i>Bandslam</i> was commercially unsuccessful, Hudgens's performance received praise from critics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> David Waddington of the <i>North Wales Pioneer</i> noted that Hudgens "outshines the rest of the cast, failing to fit in with the outcast narrative and making the inevitable climactic ending all the more expected",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> and Philip French of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> compared her acting to <a href="/wiki/Thandie_Newton" title="Thandie Newton">Thandie Newton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dorothy_Parker" title="Dorothy Parker">Dorothy Parker</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> Hudgens made a return to theater productions and starred in the musical <i><a href="/wiki/Rent_(musical)" title="Rent (musical)">Rent</a></i> as Mimi. The stage production ran from August 6–8, 2010 at the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Bowl" title="Hollywood Bowl">Hollywood Bowl</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-broadwayv_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-broadwayv-44">[44]</a></sup> Her involvement in the production drew negative comments, but director <a href="/wiki/Neil_Patrick_Harris" title="Neil Patrick Harris">Neil Patrick Harris</a> defended his decision with casting Hudgens by saying, "Vanessa [Hudgens] is awesome. She's a friend. I asked her to come in and sing to make sure she had the chops for it. And she was very committed and seemed great."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hudgens' involvement in <i><a href="/wiki/Beastly_(film)" title="Beastly (film)">Beastly</a></i>, a film based on <a href="/wiki/Alex_Flinn" title="Alex Flinn">Alex Flinn</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Beastly" title="Beastly">novel of the same name</a>, was announced in early 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> She played one of the main characters in the film, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Linda_Owens" title="Linda Owens">Linda Taylor</a>. Hudgens described her as, "...the "beauty" of the story but not the stereotypical beauty everyone thinks of."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> Along with <i>Beastly</i> co-star, Alex Pettyfer, Hudgens was recognized as <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ShoWest" title="ShoWest">ShoWest</a></i> stars of Tomorrow.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tomorrow_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-tomorrow-48">[48]</a></sup> <i>Beastly</i>, which also starred <a href="/wiki/Mary-Kate_Olsen" title="Mary-Kate Olsen">Mary-Kate Olsen</a>, was released on March 4, 2011. <i>Beastly</i> received mostly negative reviews, earning a 20% approval rating from <a href="/wiki/Rotten_Tomatoes" title="Rotten Tomatoes">Rotten Tomatoes</a> from 89 reviews, with an average rating of 3.7/10. It was ranked No. 45 in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span> predicted "50 Biggest Movies of 2010".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> The film was screened at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ShoWest" title="ShoWest">ShoWest</a> and it drew enthusiastic reactions from the luncheon crowd of exhibition officials.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> The film went on to make $28 million worldwide as of 2012. Hudgens was also cast as one of the five female leads in the action film <i><a href="/wiki/Sucker_Punch_(2011_film)" title="Sucker Punch (2011 film)">Sucker Punch</a></i>, directed by <a href="/wiki/Zack_Snyder" title="Zack Snyder">Zack Snyder</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> She played Blondie, an institutionalized girl in an asylum. The film was released in March 2011,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> and grossed $19 million in its first weekend at the North American box office, opening at number two.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boxofficecemojo_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-boxofficecemojo-54">[54]</a></sup> By the end of its run, <i>Sucker Punch</i> totaled $89 million worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BoxOfficeMojo_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-BoxOfficeMojo-55">[55]</a></sup> Though the film's content was derided, it received some recognition for the visual effects of the fantasy sequences. <i>Sucker Punch</i> received a nomination at the <a href="/wiki/2011_Scream_Awards" title="2011 Scream Awards">2011 Scream Awards</a> for Best F/X, and its <a href="/wiki/Stunt" title="Stunt">stunt work</a> was nominated for a <a href="/wiki/Taurus_World_Stunt_Awards" title="Taurus World Stunt Awards">Taurus Award</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vanessa_Hudgens_PCA_2012.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="494" data-file-width="382" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Vanessa_Hudgens_PCA_2012.jpg/170px-Vanessa_Hudgens_PCA_2012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Vanessa_Hudgens_PCA_2012.jpg/255px-Vanessa_Hudgens_PCA_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Vanessa_Hudgens_PCA_2012.jpg/340px-Vanessa_Hudgens_PCA_2012.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vanessa_Hudgens_PCA_2012.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hudgens at the 2012 <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Choice_Awards" title="People's Choice Awards">People's Choice Awards</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In October 2010, Hudgens joined the cast of <i><a href="/wiki/Journey_2:_The_Mysterious_Island" title="Journey 2: The Mysterious Island">Journey 2: The Mysterious Island</a></i> (2012), the sequel to the 2008 film <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Journey_to_the_Center_of_the_Earth_(2008_Hollywood_film)" title="Journey to the Center of the Earth (2008 Hollywood film)">Journey to the Center of the Earth</a></i>, alongside <a href="/wiki/Dwayne_Johnson" title="Dwayne Johnson">Dwayne Johnson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Josh_Hutcherson" title="Josh Hutcherson">Josh Hutcherson</a>, playing Hutcherson's love interest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> The film earned $325 million worldwide during its theatrical run,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> which outperformed its predecessor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> It received generally mixed to negative reviews from critics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reviews_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reviews-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> The consensus from Rotten Tomatoes is: "Aggressively unambitious, <i>Journey 2</i> might thrill teen viewers, but most others will find it too intense for young audiences and too cartoonishly dull for adults".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reviews_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-Reviews-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>In November 2011, Hudgens announced on her official website that she would be starring with <a href="/wiki/Selena_Gomez" title="Selena Gomez">Selena Gomez</a> and <a href="/wiki/James_Franco" title="James Franco">James Franco</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Spring_Breakers" title="Spring Breakers">Spring Breakers</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> The film followed four college-aged girls who decide to rob a fast food restaurant in order to pay for their spring break.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rachel_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rachel-64">[64]</a></sup> It was released theatrically in March 2013,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> receiving generally positive reviews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> The film featured mature themes such as drug use, sexual escapades, and violence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> To coincide with the film, Hudgens later released the dubstep influenced song "$$$ex",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> with a music video featuring clips from the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> The song features guest vocals from YLA, and was produced by <a href="/wiki/Rock_Mafia" title="Rock Mafia">Rock Mafia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>In April 2011, it was reported that she would star in <i><a href="/wiki/Gimme_Shelter_(2013_film)" title="Gimme Shelter (2013 film)">Gimme Shelter</a></i> with <a href="/wiki/Brendan_Fraser" title="Brendan Fraser">Brendan Fraser</a>, a film written and directed by Ron Krauss.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Hudgens also plays Cindy Paulson in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Frozen_Ground" title="The Frozen Ground">The Frozen Ground</a></i> (2013), a film based on the <a href="/wiki/Robert_Hansen" title="Robert Hansen">Robert Hansen</a> case wherein she plays as his only victim who escaped. She co-stars with <a href="/wiki/John_Cusack" title="John Cusack">John Cusack</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Cage" title="Nicolas Cage">Nicolas Cage</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2015.E2.80.93present:_Broadway_and_Powerless">2015–present: Broadway and <i>Powerless</i></span></h3>
<p>In 2015, Hudgens took on the title role in the new production of <a href="/wiki/Alan_Jay_Lerner" title="Alan Jay Lerner">Alan Jay Lerner</a> and <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Loewe" title="Frederick Loewe">Frederick Loewe</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Gigi_(musical)" title="Gigi (musical)">Gigi</a></i>, which opened at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kennedy_Center" title="Kennedy Center">Kennedy Center</a> from January 16 to February 12,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> before transferring to <a href="/wiki/Broadway_theatre" title="Broadway theatre">Broadway</a> on April 8.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> The production closed on June 21.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p>On January 31, 2016, Hudgens starred in the coveted role of Rizzo in <i><a href="/wiki/Grease:_Live" title="Grease: Live">Grease: Live</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company" title="Fox Broadcasting Company">Fox's</a> live broadcast based on the <a href="/wiki/Grease_(musical)" title="Grease (musical)">original Broadway musical</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-grease_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-grease-80">[80]</a></sup> Hudgens dedicated her performance to her father, Greg, who died from cancer one day before the special aired.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hudgens was cast in a pilot for a TV comedy series titled <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Powerless_(TV_Pilot)" title="Powerless (TV Pilot)">Powerless</a></i>, which is based on <a href="/wiki/DC_Comics" title="DC Comics">DC Comics</a> characters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vanessa_Hudgens_and_Josh_Hutcherson_(6718742151).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="1000" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Vanessa_Hudgens_and_Josh_Hutcherson_%286718742151%29.jpg/170px-Vanessa_Hudgens_and_Josh_Hutcherson_%286718742151%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Vanessa_Hudgens_and_Josh_Hutcherson_%286718742151%29.jpg/255px-Vanessa_Hudgens_and_Josh_Hutcherson_%286718742151%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Vanessa_Hudgens_and_Josh_Hutcherson_%286718742151%29.jpg/340px-Vanessa_Hudgens_and_Josh_Hutcherson_%286718742151%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vanessa_Hudgens_and_Josh_Hutcherson_(6718742151).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hudgens and <a href="/wiki/Josh_Hutcherson" title="Josh Hutcherson">Josh Hutcherson</a> in January 2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Hudgens began a relationship with <i><a href="/wiki/High_School_Musical" title="High School Musical">High School Musical</a></i> co-star <a href="/wiki/Zac_Efron" title="Zac Efron">Zac Efron</a> in 2005. The couple became a frequent target for the media, and in turn the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> predicted that Hudgens would be a "household name" in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> They ended their relationship after five years in December 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> Hudgens is very close friends with actress <a href="/wiki/Ashley_Tisdale" title="Ashley Tisdale">Ashley Tisdale</a>, whom she met when they both starred in the film <i>High School Musical;</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> Hudgens was a bridesmaid at Tisdale's wedding on September 8, 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hudgens has been in a relationship with actor <a href="/wiki/Austin_Butler" title="Austin Butler">Austin Butler</a> since 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2016, Hudgens paid $1,000 in restitution for damage of <a href="/wiki/United_States_Forest_Service" title="United States Forest Service">U.S. Forest Service</a> property by carving the initials of her and Butler's names within a heart on a rock in the <a href="/wiki/Coconino_National_Forest" title="Coconino National Forest">Coconino National Forest</a> and displaying it on her personal <a href="/wiki/Instagram" title="Instagram">Instagram</a> feed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> Hudgens was raised Catholic, but did not feel connected to that denomination of Christianity. She is a non-denomination Christian and often attends Hillsongs Church.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Leaked_photos">Leaked photos</span></h3>
<p>On September 6, 2007, photos of Hudgens appeared online, one showing her posing in <a href="/wiki/Lingerie" title="Lingerie">lingerie</a> and another showing her nude. A statement from her publicist claims that the photo was taken privately and it was unfortunate that they were released on the Internet. Hudgens later apologized, saying that she was "embarrassed over the situation" and regretted having "taken [those] photos".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> Hudgens subsequently released a statement indicating that she declined to comment further on the subject.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/OK!" title="OK!">OK!</a></i> magazine speculated that Hudgens would be dropped from <i>High School Musical 3</i> as a result of the images,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> but <a href="/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Company" title="The Walt Disney Company">The Walt Disney Company</a> denied this, saying, "Vanessa has apologized for what was obviously a lapse in judgment. We hope she's learned a valuable lesson."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<p>In August 2009, another set of pictures showing Hudgens topless emerged on the Internet. Hudgens' representatives did not comment, though her lawyers requested the removal of the pictures from the Internet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> In late 2009, Hudgens sued "www.moejackson.com" for posting nude "self-portrait photographs" of her taken on a mobile phone in a private home.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> Hudgens later commented on the photos' impact on her career in the October issue of <i><a href="/wiki/Allure_(magazine)" title="Allure (magazine)">Allure</a></i> with, "Whenever anybody asks me, would I do nudity in a film, if I say that it's something I'm not comfortable with, they're like, 'Bullshit, you've already done it.' If anything, it makes it more embarrassing, because that was a private thing. It's screwed up that someone screwed me over like that. At least some people are learning from my mistake."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> According to <i><a href="/wiki/Us_Weekly" title="Us Weekly">Us Weekly</a></i>, further pictures were released on the Internet on March 15, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_image">Public image</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vanessa_Hudgens_Bondi_Beach_4.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2510" data-file-width="1676" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Vanessa_Hudgens_Bondi_Beach_4.jpg/170px-Vanessa_Hudgens_Bondi_Beach_4.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Vanessa_Hudgens_Bondi_Beach_4.jpg/255px-Vanessa_Hudgens_Bondi_Beach_4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Vanessa_Hudgens_Bondi_Beach_4.jpg/340px-Vanessa_Hudgens_Bondi_Beach_4.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vanessa_Hudgens_Bondi_Beach_4.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hudgens in January 2012 at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bondi_Beach,_New_South_Wales" title="Bondi Beach, New South Wales">Bondi Beach</a>, Sydney</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Hudgens was represented by <a href="/wiki/William_Morris_Agency" title="William Morris Agency">William Morris Agency</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> but signed on to <a href="/wiki/Creative_Artists_Agency" title="Creative Artists Agency">Creative Artists Agency</a> in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> In 2006, Hudgens's earnings were estimated to be $2 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> Hudgens was included in <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> richest list in early 2007, and the <i>Forbes</i> article noted that she was included in <i>Young Hollywood's Top Earning-Stars</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> On December 12, 2008, Hudgens was ranked No. 20 in the list of <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> "High Earners Under 30", having reported to have an estimated earnings of $3 million in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Forbes-December2008_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes-December2008-109">[109]</a></sup> She was number 62 at <i><a href="/wiki/FHM" title="FHM">FHM</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s Sexiest Women in the World of 2008 and number 42 in the 2009 list.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> Hudgens is also featured in <i><a href="/wiki/Maxim_(magazine)" title="Maxim (magazine)">Maxim</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s lists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> She was included in <i><a href="/wiki/People_(magazine)" title="People (magazine)">People</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'s</span> annual "100 Most Beautiful People" 2008 and 2009 lists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hudgens promotes <a href="/wiki/Neutrogena" title="Neutrogena">Neutrogena</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> and was the 2008 featured celebrity for <a href="/wiki/Sears" title="Sears">Sears</a>' back-to school campaign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> In 2007, she became a spokesperson for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marc_Eck%C5%8D" title="Marc Eckō">Marc Eckō</a> products but ended the contract after two years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> Hudgens regularly volunteers for charitable activities, including those for <a href="/wiki/Best_Buddies_International" title="Best Buddies International">Best Buddies International</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> Lollipop Theater Network,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/St._Jude_Children%27s_Research_Hospital" title="St. Jude Children's Research Hospital">St. Jude Children's Research Hospital</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VH1_Save_The_Music_Foundation" title="VH1 Save The Music Foundation">VH1 Save The Music Foundation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> Hudgens is also featured in <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A_Very_Special_Christmas_Vol.7" title="A Very Special Christmas Vol.7">A Very Special Christmas Vol.7</a></i> disc which benefits the <a href="/wiki/Special_Olympics" title="Special Olympics">Special Olympics</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> Hudgens is also part of the "Stand Up to Cancer (SU2C): Change The Odds" along with other Hollywood stars including Zac Efron, <a href="/wiki/Dakota_Fanning" title="Dakota Fanning">Dakota Fanning</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kristen_Bell" title="Kristen Bell">Kristen Bell</a>, and others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brian Schall sued Hudgens in 2007 for an alleged "breach of contract"; according to the suit, Schall claims he advanced costs and expenses on Hudgens' behalf for her songwriting and recording career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> Schall claims Hudgens owed him $150,000 after helping her earn more than $5 million for her music career. Hudgens argued that she was a 16-year-old <a href="/wiki/Minor_(law)" title="Minor (law)">minor</a> when she signed the contract in October 2005, and therefore too young to do so. She subsequently disaffirmed it on October 9, 2008. Papers filed in court by her lawyer say California's Family Code "provides that the contract of a minor is voidable and may be disaffirmed before (age 18) or within a reasonable time afterward."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> In 2008, Hudgens was sued by Johnny Vieira, who claims he was owed a share of Hudgens' advances, royalties and merchandising revenue in exchange for his management services. Vieira accuses Hudgens of abandoning her talent team as soon as she became a commercial name.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> In early May 2009, the case was settled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
